tridagon-link (horiz, same row) for digits 7, 8 and 9 in blocks:
        b3, with cells: r2c9 (link cell), r3c7, r1c8

        b9, with cells: r7c9, r9c7, r8c8

 ==> tridagon-link[12](n4r2c9, n6r2c1)
tridagon-forcing-whip-elim[13] based on tridagon-link(n4r2c9, n6r2c1)
....for n4r2c9: -
....for n6r2c1: partial-whip[1]: r2c6{n6 n8} -
 ==> r2c9≠8
tridagon-forcing-whip-elim[14] based on tridagon-link(n4r2c9, n6r2c1)
....for n4r2c9: -
....for n6r2c1: partial-whip[2]: r1n6{c2 c5} - c5n5{r1 r2} -
 ==> r2c5≠4, r1c7≠4
whip[1]: b3n4{r2c9 .} ==> r2c4≠4
tridagon-forcing-whip-elim[14] based on tridagon-link(n6r2c1, n4r2c9)
....for n6r2c1: -
....for n4r2c9: partial-whip[2]: c7n4{r2 r5} - r5n2{c7 c1} -
 ==> r5c1≠6

The end is in W11.

THIS IS THE PUZZLE THAT WILL NOW BE SOLVED.
DON''T FORGET TO DO THE RELEVANT DIGIT REPLACEMENTS AT THE END, based on the original givens.

Code: Select all
whip[1]: r6n7{c9 .} ==> r5c7≠7, r4c9≠7
whip[1]: b8n7{r9c6 .} ==> r2c6≠7
finned-x-wing-in-rows: n9{r9 r3}{c7 c6} ==> r2c6≠9
whip[1]: c6n9{r9 .} ==> r7c5≠9
finned-x-wing-in-columns: n9{c8 c3}{r1 r6} ==> r6c1≠9
whip[1]: r6n9{c9 .} ==> r4c9≠9, r5c7≠9
z-chain[4]: r1c3{n7 n9} - r1c8{n9 n8} - r3c7{n8 n9} - r9c7{n9 .} ==> r1c7≠7
z-chain[4]: r1c3{n9 n7} - r1c8{n7 n8} - b9n8{r8c8 r7c9} - b9n9{r7c9 .} ==> r1c7≠9
whip[4]: r2n4{c7 c9} - c9n7{r2 r6} - c9n9{r6 r7} - r9c7{n9 .} ==> r2c7≠7
z-chain[5]: c1n6{r1 r2} - r2c6{n6 n8} - r8n8{c6 c8} - r1c8{n8 n7} - r1c3{n7 .} ==> r1c1≠9
z-chain[5]: r1c3{n9 n7} - r1c8{n7 n8} - b9n8{r8c8 r7c9} - b9n9{r7c9 r9c7} - r3n9{c7 .} ==> r1c4≠9, r1c5≠9
z-chain[5]: r9c7{n9 n7} - r3c7{n7 n8} - r3c2{n8 n7} - r1c3{n7 n9} - c8n9{r1 .} ==> r6c7≠9
biv-chain[3]: r6n9{c8 c9} - r7c9{n9 n8} - r8c8{n8 n7} ==> r6c8≠7
biv-chain[3]: r6n7{c9 c7} - r9c7{n7 n9} - r7c9{n9 n8} ==> r6c9≠8
z-chain[4]: r1c3{n7 n9} - c8n9{r1 r6} - r6c9{n9 n7} - r2n7{c9 .} ==> r1c5≠7, r1c4≠7
biv-chain[3]: r1c4{n8 n4} - c5n4{r1 r8} - c5n2{r8 r3} ==> r3c5≠8
biv-chain[5]: c8n7{r1 r8} - r8c6{n7 n8} - r2c6{n8 n6} - r1n6{c5 c1} - b1n3{r1c1 r1c2} ==> r1c2≠7
hidden-pairs-in-a-row: r1{n7 n9}{c3 c8} ==> r1c8≠8
biv-chain[3]: b6n9{r6c9 r6c8} - c8n8{r6 r8} - r7c9{n8 n9} ==> r2c9≠9
biv-chain[3]: b6n7{r6c7 r6c9} - c9n9{r6 r7} - r9c7{n9 n7} ==> r3c7≠7
biv-chain[3]: r3c2{n7 n8} - r3c7{n8 n9} - r1c8{n9 n7} ==> r1c3≠7
singles ==> r1c3=9, r1c8=7, r8c8=8, r6c8=9, r6c9=7, r7c9=9, r9c7=7, r9c6=9,  r8c6=7, r3c2=7
naked-pairs-in-a-row: r2{c1 c6}{n6 n8} ==> r2c9≠8, r2c7≠8, r2c5≠8, r2c5≠6, r2c4≠8
stte

Re: The hardest sudokus (new thread)

by mith » Sat Apr 23, 2022 3:43 am

Yes, SER reduces to 8.3 after replacement.

An alternate path using an extended trivalue oddagon:

Code: Select all
. . * | . . . | . * .
a . . | . . b | . . c
. * . | . . . | * . .
------+-------+------
. . . | . . . | . . .
. . . | . . . | . . .
. . . | . . . | . . .
------+-------+------
* . . | . . . | . . *
. * . | . . * | . * .
. . * | . . * | * . .


After basics: If a is not 6, c is not 789 by trivalue oddagon in b1379. If a is 6, b is 8, and the extended pattern b1379+c6 is also not three colorable so c is again not 789. (Pretty simple after 4r2c9.)
mith

Finally found some 39c 11.7s:

Code: Select all
.....1.23..2.3.1.4..1.4256....21.64.14..653.262.4.3....731.6...21.....368963.4...  ED=11.7/11.7/8.3
.....1.23..2.3.1.4..1.4256....21.64.14..653.262.3.4....731.6...21.....368964.3...  ED=11.7/11.7/8.3
.....1.23..2.3.1.4..1.4256....21.64.14..653.262.3.4....761.3...21.....368934.6...  ED=11.7/11.7/8.3


(same puzzle other than some rectangle swaps)

Guardians in opposing boxes, but they collapse pretty quickly with the strong link:

5r6c3 = r4c123 - r4c9 =[to789b2356] = r1c5 - r789c5 = r8c4 => -5r8c3 (solvable with turbot fish from here)

Also noticed that occasionally the same puzzle is getting added to the database twice - presumably a timing thing between the scripts. Will have to figure out where that is happening, but fortunately not frequent and quick to find all the instances and remove duplicates.

Re: The hardest sudokus (new thread)

by eleven » Mon May 16, 2022 10:22 am

Impressing list.

From the solving point of view there seem to be only 4 different groups in the 11.8's (did not look at all of them). All had a single extra candidate, which
- creates a single (bivalue), and gets trivial
- creates a hidden single and gets easy (ER 5.3 - 3 strong links)
- creates a pair, and gets easy (ER 5.3)
- creates a bivalue single and leaves a ER 9.2 with a [edit:] 14c pattern, which simplifies it to ER 5.4
